          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

QuickAnswersUiController has a pointer to a View which is owned by the hierarchy, as the comment says.



<span class="line"><!---->QuickAnswersUiController has a pointer to a View which is owned by the hierarchy, as the comment says.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





But then it uses that pointer without somehow observing if the pointer is deleted, causing a UAF. This requires pretty reasonable user interaction so not decreasing the impact. The pointer in question has been present for a year now, so on all released browsers.



<span class="line"><!---->But then it uses that pointer without somehow observing if the pointer is deleted, causing a UAF. This requires pretty reasonable user interaction so not decreasing the impact. The pointer in question has been present for a year now, so on all released browsers.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Interestingly, this would potentially be mitigated by raw_ptr, if it ships, but this was missed in the raw_ptr rewrite: 



<span class="line"><!---->Interestingly, this would potentially be mitigated by raw_ptr, if it ships, but this was missed in the raw_ptr rewrite: <!----></span>





https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1299932



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1299932"><!---->https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1299932<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





I can not repro on Linux, as the given UI element does not pop up. So I will have to ask the related team to have a look. If this is not in M96 please update.



<span class="line"><!---->I can not repro on Linux, as the given UI element does not pop up. So I will have to ask the related team to have a look. If this is not in M96 please update.<!----></span>

This UAF happens because the code assumes that QuickAnswersMenuObserver::OnMenuClosed() can only happen before the QuickAnswersView itself is destroyed, but there is no guarantee of this in the presence of async window closure, and the code (as danakj@ said in #4) makes incorrect assumptions about the lifetime of the View, which it does not own.



<span class="line"><!---->This UAF happens because the code assumes that QuickAnswersMenuObserver::OnMenuClosed() can only happen before the QuickAnswersView itself is destroyed, but there is no guarantee of this in the presence of async window closure, and the code (as danakj@ said in #4) makes incorrect assumptions about the lifetime of the View, which it does not own.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In general there are a couple of ways to deal with this:



<span class="line"><!---->In general there are a couple of ways to deal with this:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1. ViewTracker instead of raw View* to hold the View (but this has a runtime cost)



<span class="line"><!---->1. ViewTracker instead of raw View* to hold the View (but this has a runtime cost)<!----></span>



<br>





2. Hold a WeakPtr to QuickAnswersView instead (it already supports WeakPtr)



<span class="line"><!---->2. Hold a WeakPtr to QuickAnswersView instead (it already supports WeakPtr)<!----></span>



<br>





3. Something else



<span class="line"><!---->3. Something else<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





QuickAnswersView is doing some unusual stuff like manually creating its own Widget as part of View construction which also makes the lifetime harder to reason about.



<span class="line"><!---->QuickAnswersView is doing some unusual stuff like manually creating its own Widget as part of View construction which also makes the lifetime harder to reason about.<!----></span>

The video is very informative that the QuickAnswersView widget could be closed by closing the browser window. So the assumption that the widget has to be closed via QuickAnswersView does not stand.



<span class="line"><!---->The video is very informative that the QuickAnswersView widget could be closed by closing the browser window. So the assumption that the widget has to be closed via QuickAnswersView does not stand.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





One quick fix could be adding a



<span class="line"><!---->One quick fix could be adding a<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





  void OnQuickAnswersViewDestroyed();



<span class="line"><!---->  void OnQuickAnswersViewDestroyed();<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





to QuickAnswersUiController and QuickAnswersView calls it from its dtor to reset the reference.



<span class="line"><!---->to QuickAnswersUiController and QuickAnswersView calls it from its dtor to reset the reference.<!----></span>

Status

(was: Fixed)


          

<br>


        




        




      

<div class="issue-diff">
        <!---->
          <strong><!---->Status:</strong>
          
          Assigned
          (was: Fixed)
          <br>
        <!---->
        
      </div>

<br>


    


        


      


        









The ASAN test failure is caused by the View outliving the Controller, being unaware the Controller has been deallocated, and trying to call a method on it. It is deeply unsafe for the Controller to hold raw pointers to Views (which it does not control the lifetime of) and for Views to hold raw pointers to the Controller (which it does not control the lifetime of).



<span class="line"><!---->The ASAN test failure is caused by the View outliving the Controller, being unaware the Controller has been deallocated, and trying to call a method on it. It is deeply unsafe for the Controller to hold raw pointers to Views (which it does not control the lifetime of) and for Views to hold raw pointers to the Controller (which it does not control the lifetime of).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I *strongly* recommend having the Views hold references to the Controller as WeakPtrs, or (if that doesn't work) having the Controller hold references to Views via ViewTracker, which provides sort of the same functionality. Doing manual pointer invalidation is fraught with peril.



<span class="line"><!---->I *strongly* recommend having the Views hold references to the Controller as WeakPtrs, or (if that doesn't work) having the Controller hold references to Views via ViewTracker, which provides sort of the same functionality. Doing manual pointer invalidation is fraught with peril.<!----></span>

<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.
